    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=pratchett-terry">pratchett-terry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320525855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14194802147795496703">Stereotyping music, its industry, and the completely overrated impact of this terrible noise disturbance played by teenagers the next house across the street or, worse, next door. Stop that or I´ll call the police, you spoiled punk brats!<br/><br/>Creative commons, social collaboration, everything sharing, Kickstarter, Patreon, all that eco social stuff I am into too, etc. are all things Pratchett promotes indirectly by criticizing monopolies, dealers of content, <br/>swivelers of adhesion contracts who give c</span>
  <span id="freeText14194802147795496703" style="display:none">Stereotyping music, its industry, and the completely overrated impact of this terrible noise disturbance played by teenagers the next house across the street or, worse, next door. Stop that or I´ll call the police, you spoiled punk brats!<br /><br />Creative commons, social collaboration, everything sharing, Kickstarter, Patreon, all that eco social stuff I am into too, etc. are all things Pratchett promotes indirectly by criticizing monopolies, dealers of content, <br />swivelers of adhesion contracts who give crumbs to the artists and the real cash to the temporary owners of their creativity, and the general mainstream plague destroying most of music, movies, series, and even books. They don´t even stop there, it´s terrible! It could also be seen as a criticism of the quality of overappreciated music itself by some, but I prefer the organized crime style music conglomerate guild hunting unlicensed musicians scheme. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Both shown as Cut Me Own-Throat Dibbler as the manager secretly hoarding gold and the musicians guild trying to get them mutilated or dead.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The magic aspect of music is there too, so let´s get fringe pop fantasy sciency. Humans can hear it and it´s a wave, it´s even vibrating a bit if it´s dosed right, and we know close to nothing about physics and the universe. So why can´t it be that the effect of altogether, the words, possibly magic and hypnotizing effects, the right combination of notes like a code to manipulate physics, and the already existing abilities of the singer and the instruments, open up parallel universes, anomalies, haunt, invoke demons and angels, change reality, and assist and motivate during boring routine household activities. <br /><br />That´s not just meant as a joke, just the impact of dancing, singing, and instruments in many cultish actions, be it institutionalized, satanic, indigenous peoples with drugs, or the equivalent in the form or a rave, beer tent, or music festival, should let one think. The participants, already stoned as hell, have their epiphanies, visions, etc., so it´s real for them, possibly even lifechanging or at least endangering. Would be pretty arrogant to say that there is nothing special about the mixture of annoying catastrophic cacophonic caterwauling and the mentioned influences. Just a pity that we have so few senses and reduced perceptiveness, more sensible humans or aliens might get even more out of it or directly interact with whatever.<br /><br />DEATH is having one more of his midlife, endless life crisis, cry for attention crisis,… that dude should seriously consider a career change, it´s never too late, even after one or some eternities. Possibly something else with people or once something without, more professional gardening, something with animals, or why not try it with accounting or internal audit? „I could very well imagine you in that position.“, the human resources manager nodded towards the somewhat strange applicant. Also, his grandparenting skills are about as good as his parenting skills, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ which leads to even more forced DEATH alternatives. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As I tend to repeatedly say, I don´t know much about music and musicians, so there are certainly hidden treasures, probably for both the groups and musicians Pratchett liked himself and the very famous ones. But because I am highly susceptible to earworms, I will hardly ever be able to improve my knowledge, I even subconsciously know a bit more about the classics and ancient writings I normally use in this sentence to glorify my incompetence. I don´t rudimentarily get, for instance, the hidden innuendos of how the music influences the wizards of The Unseen university. It´s a shame.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/SoulMusic">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><br />This one is added to all Pratchettian reviews:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheibenwelt-Romane#Liste_der_Romane">https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheibe...</a> <br />The idea of the dissected motifs rocks, highlighting the main real world inspirational elements of fiction and satire is something usually done with so called higher literature, but a much more interesting field in readable literature, as it offers the joy of reading, subtle criticism, and feeling smart all together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14194802147795496703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Most of the action takes place in Ankh-Morpork but the Band also goes on tour. As in most of Pratchett’s work, this is also a satire on a great many things, most notably here commercialism, music industry, art and music, and human nature.<br><br>Fun, fun, fun.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1564075922i/27885918.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8842699307584157242"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536869217i/26298212.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Music is immortal. Some say it has always been there and always will. Some can apparently hear its beat. Like the pulse of the universe itself. I think Terry Pratchett had that same kind of appreciation for this particular art.<br/><br/>In this 16th installment of the phenomenon that is the <i>Discworld</i> series, Death has a family-related crisis so he goes away for a while. Unlike the last time, there is someone to take over though and the Death of Rats and Binky are getting her. Yes, HER. Susan, Death's gran</span>
  <span id="freeText8842699307584157242" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536869217i/26298212.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Music is immortal. Some say it has always been there and always will. Some can apparently hear its beat. Like the pulse of the universe itself. I think Terry Pratchett had that same kind of appreciation for this particular art.<br><br>In this 16th installment of the phenomenon that is the <i>Discworld</i> series, Death has a family-related crisis so he goes away for a while. Unlike the last time, there is someone to take over though and the Death of Rats and Binky are getting her. Yes, HER. Susan, Death's granddaughter (who is kinda blissfully unaware).<br>As she learns to wield the scythe as much as her unique form of memory and everything inherited from her grandfather, music arrives on the Discworld in the form of a guitar bought in a peculiar shop (think of the "woodcarver shop" in Pixar's <i>Brave</i>). It wants to be played and not by anyone. <br>Thus, we are treated to a grande tour by some ... music with rocks in it.<br><br>Along the way, we get a lot of musical references many of which even I understood *is very proud of herself* and which added to the hilarity of the absurdness unfolding in Ankh-Morpork, the Unseen University and many other places. Underwear being thrown onto the stage was the most innocent of the incidents. *snort-giggles*<br><br>A wonderful adventure through dark alleys, in stinking taverns, along sharply winding roads and up on stages that is the introduction of one of the best characters, apparently: Susan. I already liked the novel with her future father way back when, but she's even better, especially when paired with a talking raven and the Death of Rats (Binky is not to be underestimated either).<br>Though I have to say that the Librarian, Ridcully and the other wizards were marvellous, once again, as well.<br><br>Moreover, as is almost to be expected especially from the novels about Death, the author had a wonderful way of weaving pop culture references with action and, most impressively, resoundingly deep and important messages about life (and death) itself.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1536869217i/26298213.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4126263070799808604">I didn't realise I was a month behind in my (self imposed) Discworld novel per month readathon, but apparently I was/am. That said as per usual it was a thoroughly enjoyable hilarious novel.<br/><br/>I know I've said it before, but this must be one of my favourite novels so far ha ha.   <span id="freeText4126263070799808604" style="display:none">I didn't realise I was a month behind in my (self imposed) Discworld novel per month readathon, but apparently I was/am. That said as per usual it was a thoroughly enjoyable hilarious novel.<br /><br />I know I've said it before, but this must be one of my favourite novels so far ha ha. It has probably my favourite character, as in DEATH, although when I read books with The Witches, I love them, oh and of course The Night Watch, Oh blow it, all of them are just so different and so much fun.<br /><br />In this book, DEATH goes a-wandering, and his "granddaughter", Susan, Is "selected" to take his place, by higher powers. Tracked down by a talking Raven and the DEATH of RATS, she initially doesn't believe in anything supernatural. Concurrently a harpist in Ankh Morpork, buys a guitar from a shop that never used to be there and its "music magic" makes its chords and riffs irresistible to all who hear it.<br />CMOT Dibbler gets involved as a music Impresario and Susan as DEATH is also in the mix with most of the Senior Wizards from Unseen University, along with a number of Trolls as everything starts going completely wrong. Step in Albert, DEATH's "man", who realises this cannot be allowed to continue and goes in hunt of DEATH to sort the mess out.<br /><br />A wonderfully written Discworld novel, full of all the humour, pathos and characters that make the Discworld series what it is to so many avid followers.</span>

<div id="review_3559395294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3559395294" />
    <a title="Ken" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38999260-ken"><img alt="Ken" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446483502p2/38999260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3559395294?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken" href="/user/show/38999260-ken">Ken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473200128" href="/book/show/20439087-soul-music">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3559395294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11187159020772681108">Just like the subject that Prachett is parodying, Soul Music feels like a greatest hits compilation of some of the earlier Discworld novels.<br/><br/>There's lots of similarities to Reaper Man and Moving Pictures, whilst it's also great direct sequel to Mort.<br/><br/>This is only my second Discworld read of the year, so probably meant that I'd enjoyed it more - I really should pick these up more regularly.<br/>Gags about popular music is always going to be a winner for me and felt that I caught most of the references.<br/><br/>M</span>
  <span id="freeText11187159020772681108" style="display:none">Just like the subject that Prachett is parodying, Soul Music feels like a greatest hits compilation of some of the earlier Discworld novels.<br /><br />There's lots of similarities to Reaper Man and Moving Pictures, whilst it's also great direct sequel to Mort.<br /><br />This is only my second Discworld read of the year, so probably meant that I'd enjoyed it more - I really should pick these up more regularly.<br />Gags about popular music is always going to be a winner for me and felt that I caught most of the references.<br /><br />Many of the bands and songs that Prachett riffs on are so popular that it was easy to spot plenty of them, 'Cavern Deep and Mountain High' being a particular favourite!<br /><br />It was slightly disappointing that Death didnt feature too heavily in this novel, I felt a little short changed. But meeting his granddaughter Susan made up for it.<br />I actually quite like Pratchat Podcast theory that 'Susan' is a Doctor Who reference, slightly kicking myself for missing it - but shows that this series is a perfect buddy/readalong pick.<br /><br />Both the topics on how influential music is to a person whilst the struggle for exposure and touring for musicians make a perfect subject for Prachett to tackle.<br />I just wished the overarching plot was a little more unique.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11187159020772681108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1259302248" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1259302248" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259302248?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259302248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17291439420434723466">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2018. <br/><br/>Death takes a break at about the same time as the Discworld latches on to yet another passing concept from elsewhere in the multiverse: Music with Rocks In. Ankh-Morpork gets hit hard by the arrival of some new musicians and soon the whole city can't get enough of the new music, particularly including some of the Unseen University faculty. Meanwhile, with Death missing, the role is picked up by his young granddaughter, Susa</span>
  <span id="freeText17291439420434723466" style="display:none">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2018. <br /><br />Death takes a break at about the same time as the Discworld latches on to yet another passing concept from elsewhere in the multiverse: Music with Rocks In. Ankh-Morpork gets hit hard by the arrival of some new musicians and soon the whole city can't get enough of the new music, particularly including some of the Unseen University faculty. Meanwhile, with Death missing, the role is picked up by his young granddaughter, Susan Sto-Helit.<br /><br />In structure this book is very similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34517.Reaper_Man__Discworld___11__Death___2_" title="Reaper Man (Discworld, #11; Death, #2) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Reaper Man</a>, with two main plots that barely intersect. There's the Wizards dealing with the new music (including the first glimpse of what will later be called Hex) and the band that is playing it, and a parallel plot dealing with Susan and Death and their grief over Susan's parents deaths.<br /><br />Like Reaper Man, the Death plot is the star, and while it has moments of humor the way that grief is affecting both of these characters is quite profound as is the relationship that they develop because of it.<br /><br />I do think that this is a slightly lesser work in the series, if only because the A-plot is a bit pointless, and the B-plot has the heavy lifting of introducing Susan. I think the processing of grief that both Death and Susan are doing throughout is very subtle and extremely well-handled.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_452819736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452819736" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452819736?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061805752" href="/book/show/9454765-soul-music">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=anglophilia">anglophilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=musical">musical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=satire">satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=what-s-this-art-thing-all-about-yo">what-s-this-art-thing-all-about-yo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=wibbly-wobbly-timey-wimey">wibbly-wobbly-timey-wimey</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452819736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3982900406108161512"><blockquote><i>“He had the feeling, once again, that he’d missed out on something somewhere. He’d never really realized it until the last couple of days. He didn’t know what it was. He just wanted to </i>do<i> things. He didn’t know what they were. But he wanted to do them soon.”<br/><br/>“There are millions of chords. There are millions of numbers. And everyone forgets the one that is a zero. But without the zero, numbers are just arithmetic. Without the empty chord, music is just noise.”</i></blockquote><br/>It was just happenstance that the firs</span>
  <span id="freeText3982900406108161512" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>“He had the feeling, once again, that he’d missed out on something somewhere. He’d never really realized it until the last couple of days. He didn’t know what it was. He just wanted to </i>do<i> things. He didn’t know what they were. But he wanted to do them soon.”<br /><br />“There are millions of chords. There are millions of numbers. And everyone forgets the one that is a zero. But without the zero, numbers are just arithmetic. Without the empty chord, music is just noise.”</i></blockquote><br />It was just happenstance that the first Pratchett book I got to read after Sir Terry died last month is one of those that feature DEATH, and musings on, but it certainly made the experience of reading <i>Soul Music</i> more bittersweet than it would have been otherwise. It didn’t end up being my favorite Discworld book, but it’s still a reminder of what we’ve lost in losing* Terry Pratchett.<br /><br /><i>*A euphemism implying we can probably find him hiding under our beds or stuffed in the fridge next to the ketchup if only we just looked hard enough.</i><br /><br />The Discworld books don’t have to be read in order, but I have to read them that way. If you’re looking for a way in to the series, you could do worse than with this book. I feel it’s good, not great. But if you want a stellar one to start with I’d recommend <i>Guards! Guards!</i> instead, or even <i>Reaper Man</i>, which was the previous book in the DEATH sub-series. Terry Pratchett’s version of Death is an anthropomorphized, soulful, skeletal sort of guy who’s always having emotional crises, losing faith in his job, and then wandering off for a while to find himself. He also speaks IN ALL CAPITAL LETTERS.<br /><br />This time around, his crisis precipitates his granddaughter, Susan, taking over the business. Susan is a very practical girl, raised by her parents (Death’s adopted daughter and his old apprentice) to disregard anything even remotely nonsensical. While Susan is busy learning the Family Business, magical disaster is of course once again invading the Discworld, this time in the form of music. Specifically of the type “with rocks in.” Imp y Celyn (Welsh for Bud of the Holly . . . get it?) and two new acquaintances also new to the fine disaster of a city known as Ankh-Morpork decide to start a band after being rejected by the Musician’s Guild, and after finding a guitar in a Mysterious Shop that produces the most wondrous music . . .<br /><br />As they tend to do in Discworld books, the two stories converge in a manner I can only describe as “wonko,” but the twin themes of Death and Music actually work really well together, and I ended up coming out of the book sort of teary-eyed, and not just because I was thinking about its dearly departed author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3982900406108161512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_355920881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355920881" />
    <a title="Igor Ljubuncic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10471943-igor-ljubuncic"><img alt="Igor Ljubuncic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492196263p2/10471943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355920881?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Igor Ljubuncic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Igor Ljubuncic" href="/user/show/10471943-igor-ljubuncic">Igor Ljubuncic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10471943-igor-ljubuncic?shelf=terry-pratchett">terry-pratchett</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355920881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4230448300039058323">40 books on my Pratchett shelf, 40 books to review, if I write one now, there'll 39 books on my Pratchet shelf left to review.<br/><br/>But it should be interesting.<br/><br/>The way I remember it, through the first half of the DW series, Terry was busy exploring existentialism in different ways, with witches, death (and associates), a fast-running coward, the genius Night Watch (my favorite) ...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486930677i/21962114._SX540_.png' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>... before he finally nailed it. He eventually got well comfortable with his own writing, and the series picked up pace, </span>
  <span id="freeText4230448300039058323" style="display:none">40 books on my Pratchett shelf, 40 books to review, if I write one now, there'll 39 books on my Pratchet shelf left to review.<br><br>But it should be interesting.<br><br>The way I remember it, through the first half of the DW series, Terry was busy exploring existentialism in different ways, with witches, death (and associates), a fast-running coward, the genius Night Watch (my favorite) ...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486930677i/21962114._SX540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>... before he finally nailed it. He eventually got well comfortable with his own writing, and the series picked up pace, quality, humor, and depth, and he abandoned some of the darker characters. <br><br>Soul Music is a largely forgettable if fun yet slightly grim novel, which straddles the two worlds, between the initial heavy tone and the more over-arching adventure-driven second half. We have Death of course, but then we also get Susan, who replaces Mort as a sidekick. That is just the backdrop, as the main story is around a music band who almost destroys the fabric of time with their performance.<br><br>There isn't too much to say that won't be a spoiler. Soul Music is a nice piece of written work, but it does not have the punch like some of the later works, mostly because its theme is a one-off. I guess this was a turning point for Terry, although I cannot be sure he wrote the books sequently, as the books later in the series suddenly become more vibrant and interesting.<br><br>If you're a DW fan, you will like this. It has its special charm and flavor, and it's one big pun, after all.<br><br>No limerick, as this book is about music. Mwuahahahaha.<br><br>Igor</span>
  <a data-text-id="4230448300039058323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1766347362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1766347362" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766347362?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766347362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1069626801218403251">Every now and then, we get one of those “real world stuff bleeds into the Discworld” books. For example, <i>Moving Pictures</i> involved, as you might guess, a sudden discovery of and obsession about movies. With a <i>Discworld</i> flare, of course. Those books are the ones I seem to enjoy the least. <i>Soul Music</i> is the third book in the <i>Death</i> subseries, and it was one of those types of books. In this case, the sudden discovery and obsession is for rock and roll music although, in <i>Discworld</i>, it goes by the name</span>
  <span id="freeText1069626801218403251" style="display:none">Every now and then, we get one of those “real world stuff bleeds into the Discworld” books. For example, <i>Moving Pictures</i> involved, as you might guess, a sudden discovery of and obsession about movies. With a <i>Discworld</i> flare, of course. Those books are the ones I seem to enjoy the least. <i>Soul Music</i> is the third book in the <i>Death</i> subseries, and it was one of those types of books. In this case, the sudden discovery and obsession is for rock and roll music although, in <i>Discworld</i>, it goes by the name “Music with Rocks In” and includes some trolls using rocks as drums.<br /><br />Maybe part of the problem is that I just don’t seem to get a lot of the jokes in these types of books. I’ve never watched a lot of movies, so a lot of the stuff in <i>Moving Pictures</i> went over my head. Likewise, I’m not terribly knowledgeable about rock and roll, and I think most of the references were probably from the 50’s and maybe 60’s, and I’ve never listened much to the music of that era. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m embarrassed to say how long it took me before I finally got the constantly-repeated “he looks elvish” joke. I’m pretty sure I was at least halfway through the book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In addition to that, we have Death once again going off the grid and shirking his responsibilities, leaving other people to deal with the repercussions. This is only the third Death book and yet it already feels repetitive. Part of the reason it frustrates me is because Death is a fun character, and I want to see more of him actually being Death. I think I actually enjoy him more when he shows up in the other subseries books.<br /><br />I guess it sounds like I hated the book, and I really didn’t. It’s just easier to write about my complaints. So, what did I like? I enjoyed the humor that didn’t relate to rock and roll music. Pratchett has a great way of coming up with funny descriptions for common things. For example, this one made me laugh enough that I took the time to highlight it: <i>"And people got up and started cheerin’ and dancin’ and stampin’ their feet like there was a plague of cockroaches."</i>. I also really enjoyed the concept of the character of Susan, who was one of the aforementioned characters who had to take up the slack for Death. I say “the concept of” because she really didn’t get nearly enough page time and her part of the story was too similar to another story in an earlier book. Despite that, she captured my attention when she was first introduced and I really liked the idea of her character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1069626801218403251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_360418882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360418882" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4367251-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303001337p2/4367251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360418882?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/4367251-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4367251-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4367251-gavin?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4367251-gavin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360418882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5223607613238893714">Not up there with the best of his stuff, but I should point out at this juncture that since Guards Guards he's been getting marked on a scale relative only to his other books. If I'd picked up this book last week written by some po-dunk nobody it'd be getting five stars and I'd be desperately googling them for websites, blogs and news of their next release.<br/><br/>Soul Music is a slightly unbalanced pair of narratives, one about the infringing of rock and roll into the Discworld and the other a rather s</span>
  <span id="freeText5223607613238893714" style="display:none">Not up there with the best of his stuff, but I should point out at this juncture that since Guards Guards he's been getting marked on a scale relative only to his other books. If I'd picked up this book last week written by some po-dunk nobody it'd be getting five stars and I'd be desperately googling them for websites, blogs and news of their next release.<br /><br />Soul Music is a slightly unbalanced pair of narratives, one about the infringing of rock and roll into the Discworld and the other a rather sombre meditation about the toll that being Death would take upon the newly humanised Death (and the continuation of the theme through his Granddaughter, a not-yet-full-formed Susan). The Death stuff works brilliantly and is as enjoyable and thought-provoking as you'd expect, Susan is a little roughly drawn but still very engaging, however the Music with Rocks In stuff -in particular the dovetailing of the main threads at the end and pop culture referencing- makes the book feel episodic, and a little... less than it could have been.<br /><br />I should say here that I don't find pop culture references funny, I realise that there was a time that a person could come on stage and do a film quote to rapturous applause and endless plaudits, but that time is long gone. Obviously yes I realise this book is twenty (!) years old now and that there isn't really a clearly defined line as to why referencing books = Literature and referencing other media = Trash but it still doesn't work for me. Apart from the gag about the De(a)f Leopard. That was brilliant.<br /><br />These are tiny, tiny criticisms though and for all of them I still got through the thing cover to cover in two days so it should go without saying that it's un-put-down-able. Another great Discworld book, not to be missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5223607613238893714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It was fun, it was funny, and of course since it's DEATH that bumped it up a notch because his dialogue as always was spot on. I just didn't care much for the musical sub plot in the book. </span>

<div id="review_103977042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103977042" />
    <a title="Malin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3768439-malin"><img alt="Malin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357323185p2/3768439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103977042?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malin" href="/user/show/3768439-malin">Malin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552140294" href="/book/show/597033.Soul_Music">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3768439-malin?shelf=my-books">my-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3768439-malin?shelf=cbr7">cbr7</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3768439-malin?shelf=i-dare-you-to-2015">i-dare-you-to-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3768439-malin?shelf=what-an-animal-2015">what-an-animal-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3768439-malin?shelf=how-many-books-2015">how-many-books-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103977042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2896744887753343680">Susan Sto Helit goes to a boarding school, and for the lessons she's less interested in, she has a tendency to fade into the woodwork - literally. Susan has the ability to fade away, should she so wish it. Turns out, this is because her grandfather is none other than Death, and when he goes missing, Susan, as his closest relative, is required to take over his duties for a while. Being deeply pragmatic and rational, thanks to her first rate education, it takes Susan a while to be persuaded, even </span>
  <span id="freeText2896744887753343680" style="display:none">Susan Sto Helit goes to a boarding school, and for the lessons she's less interested in, she has a tendency to fade into the woodwork - literally. Susan has the ability to fade away, should she so wish it. Turns out, this is because her grandfather is none other than Death, and when he goes missing, Susan, as his closest relative, is required to take over his duties for a while. Being deeply pragmatic and rational, thanks to her first rate education, it takes Susan a while to be persuaded, even when a tiny rat skeleton with a cloak and a scythe and a talking raven, not to mention the big white horse, shows up on her doorstep.<br /><br />While Susan gets reacquainted with the family history her parents tried to keep from her, something new is sweeping through Ankh Morpork - the Music with Rocks in it. The young bard Imp Y Celyn (who looks a bit Elvish) and his band mates, Cliff the troll and Glod the dwarf become unbelievably popular in record time, thanks to the guitar Imp discovered in a mysterious little music shop shortly after he arrived in the capital. The music is something new and different, it has a beat and you can dance to it, and it makes almost everyone who hears it, completely obsessed. This includes many of the esteemed wizards at the Unseen University. Ridcully, the Arch-Chancellor a, is curious and unimpressed, and determined to get to the bottom of what is making his faculty and the majority of citizens in the city to behave so strangely. <br /><br /> <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/597033.Soul_Music__Discworld___16_" title="Soul Music (Discworld, #16) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Soul Music</a> was the very first <i>Discworld</i> novel I ever read. I found it at my local library, which in the mid-90s didn't really have all that many English books and certainly not a great selection of fantasy. The unusual and colourful cover appealed to me and I suspect the blurb on the back made me curious. The book came out in 94, and since I read the trade paperback, I must have discovered <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a> sometime after 1995, probably before I'd even started high school. It was a completely different reading experience for me. I remember that I kept reading until far later than was sensible on a school night, because the book didn't have chapters, and as such, it was difficult to force myself to put the book down and stop. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/597033.Soul_Music__Discworld___16_" title="Soul Music (Discworld, #16) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Soul Music</a> is not one of the greatest <i>Discworld</i> books, but it will always hold a special place in my heart, because it was my first introduction to the writing of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>.<br /><br />I was still at work, getting everything ready for my lessons the next day, when my husband called to tell me that Terry Pratchett had died. I'm not ashamed to say, I burst into tears. Of course I knew that it would only be a matter of time, as he suffered from Alzheimer's and had always been very open about wanting to choose his own time to die, but it was still a shock. I cried for quite some time before I was able to return to my duties, and kept bursting into tears on and off for days afterwards, every time I read something online about him and the impact his writing made on so many people. It's the strongest I've been affected by the death of a celebrity, someone I never actually knew personally.<br /><br />I feel lucky and privileged that I got to meet Pratchett at signings, more than once. My husband has a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386282.Good_Omens" title="Good Omens by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Omens</a>, which is signed by both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a>, which, considering Gaiman didn't do signings in the UK all that often, makes us cherish the book for more than just being probably the best book they both wrote. Before he got diagnosed with Alzheimer's, Pratchett would pretty much do a UK signing tour every year. He apparently joked once that it was more unusual to find an unsigned copy of his books than one with his signature in it, but I still think the times that I got to see him, and exchange a few words with him were very special. One of the dwarfs in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34498.The_Truth__Discworld___25_" title="The Truth (Discworld, #25) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Truth</a> is called Gunilla, which is my middle name. When I mentioned this to him at a signing, he smiled and said: "Then you probably know what gender that dwarf is."<br /><br />Pratchett was a wonderful, important writer and in his <i>Discworld</i> books he managed to satirise so many important issues in our society. In some of his books, he is more angry than funny, but until the last few books of his career, when his brain had really started to go, he is a master of language, of plot construction and of wit. His books have made me howl with laughter, and cry buckets. A few of my favourite books of his, are non-<i>Discworld</i>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386282.Good_Omens" title="Good Omens by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Omens</a>, which I have already mentioned, was co-written with Neil Gaiman and is an amazing take on the apocalypse. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2424593.Nation" title="Nation by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Nation</a> is a YA novel that looks at identity, belief, prejudice and cross-cultural understanding. While he may have been writing in the comedic fantasy genre, that doesn't mean that he didn't have very profound things to say. We are lucky that he was a very prolific writer, so there is a great literary legacy remaining now that he's gone. RIP Terry Pratchett. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2896744887753343680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer979811217867712291"><b>Remain In Print <br/>Sir Terry Pratchett <br/>1948 - 2015</b><br/><br/>Once upon a time I was given a book voucher from my school and with that book voucher I went straight out and made sure I could actually own a Discworld novel rather than having to go to the library. It just so happened to be that small window in time when I would have preferred a Disc novel about music with rocks in than one with moving pictures, and so for a while Soul Music was my favourite book about life on Disc.<br/><br/>I went on to criticise the anima</span>
  <span id="freeText979811217867712291" style="display:none"><b>Remain In Print <br />Sir Terry Pratchett <br />1948 - 2015</b><br /><br />Once upon a time I was given a book voucher from my school and with that book voucher I went straight out and made sure I could actually own a Discworld novel rather than having to go to the library. It just so happened to be that small window in time when I would have preferred a Disc novel about music with rocks in than one with moving pictures, and so for a while Soul Music was my favourite book about life on Disc.<br /><br />I went on to criticise the animated movie based on this book for losing the magic of the prose. Turns out I had no idea what I was talking about and Soul Music the book is as lacking in the magic and the intellect as Soul Music the movie.<br /><br />Essentially following the same plot as for Moving Pictures, magic from another world invades the Disc causing obsession amongst the residents that could lead to the end of the world only for an intrepid hero to save the day, this sixteenth entry in the series feels empty, an excuse for pushing puns beyond their breaking point and making really obvious jokes about rock n roll seemingly from the point of view of somebody who doesn't <i>really</i> understand the appeal of the music.<br /><br />Sure, there's a bit about Death and his granddaughter Susan and the evolution of Ponder Stibbons in the High Energy Magic building of Unseen University but there's very little else going on here.</span>

<div id="review_1257088890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257088890" />
    <a title="Tanya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya"><img alt="Tanya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602837639p2/15698555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257088890?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya" href="/user/show/15698555-tanya">Tanya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473200128" href="/book/show/20439087-soul-music">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257088890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9622107242924922545"><b>It's lawless. It changes people. <br/>It's called Music With Rocks In.</b><br/><br/>This is the sixteenth novel in the Discworld series, and the third in the Death series. <br/><br/><i>Soul Music</i> is all about sex, drugs, and rock'n'roll—Discworld style. <br/>Well... one out of three ain’t bad. Actually, it’s only thirty-three percent, but it could be worse.<br/><br/>With Pratchett's Death being one of my all-time favorite literary characters, it's always been kind of surprising to me that the novels <i>centered</i> around Death never blow me away. </span>
  <span id="freeText9622107242924922545" style="display:none"><b>It's lawless. It changes people. <br />It's called Music With Rocks In.</b><br /><br />This is the sixteenth novel in the Discworld series, and the third in the Death series. <br /><br /><i>Soul Music</i> is all about sex, drugs, and rock'n'roll—Discworld style. <br />Well... one out of three ain’t bad. Actually, it’s only thirty-three percent, but it could be worse.<br /><br />With Pratchett's Death being one of my all-time favorite literary characters, it's always been kind of surprising to me that the novels <i>centered</i> around Death never blow me away. I much prefer him as a side-character. Because, you see—the premise with Death stories is always the same. You can bank on him having an emotional crisis, losing faith in his Duty™, and then wandering off for a while to find himself—and this time, the storylines kind of had to do backflips to converge at the end. And to be honest, I didn't fully get it. Other than the narratives feeling very unbalanced, I can't say exactly what was wrong with it, but it just fell a bit flat for me. Maybe I'm just not a fan of when our world bleeds into Discworld <i>this</i> much, making for an overly pop-culture-laden story—this one reminded me a little of <i>Moving Pictures</i>, which I also enjoyed, but was overall a bit on the forgettable side.<br /><br />The humor though, as always, is delightfully Terry, and if you love Rock music, it's full of little nods that are sometimes maybe just a little too on-your-nose: Like Imp y Celyn being Welsh for "bud of Holly", and him being constantly asked whether he's elvis(h). For all I know, he could've written this book simply for the opportunity of inserting a "grateful Death" joke (which was admittedly hilarious).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"A voice said: One. One. One, two. One, two. Then the footsteps went back into the distance. After a while, another voice said: One, two, three, four- And the universe came into being. It was wrong to call it a big bang. That would just be noise, and all that noise could create is more noise and a cosmos full of random particles. Matter exploded into being, apparently as chaos, but in fact as a chord. The ultimate power chord. Everything, all together, streaming out in one huge rush that contained within itself, like reverse fossils, everything that it was going to be. And, zigzagging through the expanding cloud, alive, that first wild live music. This had shape. It had spin. It had rhythm. It had a beat, and you could dance to it. Everything did."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />—————<br /><br /><i>All my book reviews can be found <a href="https://watercolorstain.wordpress.com/reviews-by-title/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> · Buy on <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Soul-Music-Terry-Pratchett/9781473200128?a_aid=watercolorstain" rel="nofollow noopener">BookDepository</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9622107242924922545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1054746956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1054746956" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386404-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351707681p2/8386404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1054746956?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1054746956" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3941461700444296268">6.5/10<br/><br/>Another solid entry into the Discworld series and the Death sub series (although Death has a relatively small amount of screen time) which this time tackles Rock 'n Roll coming to the Discworld. I love Rock 'n Roll and I enjoy humour so what's not to like?<br/><br/>The book started really well and got two differing strands of story line going, one with Rock 'n Roll and the other with Death going AWOL so his Granddaughter, Susan, has to take up the mantle and start to run the show. As the story progr</span>
  <span id="freeText3941461700444296268" style="display:none">6.5/10<br /><br />Another solid entry into the Discworld series and the Death sub series (although Death has a relatively small amount of screen time) which this time tackles Rock 'n Roll coming to the Discworld. I love Rock 'n Roll and I enjoy humour so what's not to like?<br /><br />The book started really well and got two differing strands of story line going, one with Rock 'n Roll and the other with Death going AWOL so his Granddaughter, Susan, has to take up the mantle and start to run the show. As the story progressed I became more involved with the Death story line and Susan became quite the character to read about. There was the usual overlapping of the two threads by the end and things tied up nicely. <br /><br />Terry Pratchett throws in the usual jokes about the subject matter with the residents of Discworld not quite getting it or making it slightly different to our own know how which produces the funnier moments in this book. The "music with rocks in it" joke became a bit stall after cropping up once every ten pages or so though. <br /><br />I think the best way to describe this one is enjoyable but forgettable. Worth the read but not worth starting this series with.<br /><br />If you like this try: "Island of the Sequined Love Nun" by Christopher Moore</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12509366434281979328">19 Feb 2008<br/>20 Jun 2014<br/>25 Aug 2016<br/><br/>Death takes a sort of holiday, so the Death of Rats goes looking for Death's granddaughter to fill the gap. Susan is off in boarding school, being an unusually practical teenager with no memory of her grandfather, when she gets the message. Meanwhile a bard, a troll, and a dwarf meet up and form a band and a magical guitar introduces the idea of Music with Rocks in to the Discworld.<br/><br/>The magic that is unleashed has more to do with lampooning record company contract</span>
  <span id="freeText12509366434281979328" style="display:none">19 Feb 2008<br />20 Jun 2014<br />25 Aug 2016<br /><br />Death takes a sort of holiday, so the Death of Rats goes looking for Death's granddaughter to fill the gap. Susan is off in boarding school, being an unusually practical teenager with no memory of her grandfather, when she gets the message. Meanwhile a bard, a troll, and a dwarf meet up and form a band and a magical guitar introduces the idea of Music with Rocks in to the Discworld.<br /><br />The magic that is unleashed has more to do with lampooning record company contracts than the typical fantasy, with room for plenty of puns, an hilarious tour, and some profound thoughts on what music means to people (interpreted broadly). And also, lots of silly business with the Death of Rats and Quoth, a raven. Funny as anything, and never mean-spirited.<br /><br />These books get even better with age, both mine and theirs.<br /><br />personal copy</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11601336864228795829"><b>Rock n Roll invades the Discworld</b><br/>26 July 2014<br/><br/>	Well, I can't believe that I have just finished my 16th Terry Pratchett Discworld novel, and that is over two years (no, not sixteen books in two years, 16 Discworld novels in two years) since I decided that I would give Pratchett the benefit of the doubt and actually read them again prior to writing up a commentary, and this isn't even the last of the Discworld novels on my 'to read' list (I think there are another six, which would bring it up to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47994.The_Last_Continent__Discworld___22__Rincewind__6_' title='The Last Continent (Discworld, #22; Rincewind #6) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Th</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11601336864228795829" style="display:none"><b>Rock n Roll invades the Discworld</b><br>26 July 2014<br><br>	Well, I can't believe that I have just finished my 16th Terry Pratchett Discworld novel, and that is over two years (no, not sixteen books in two years, 16 Discworld novels in two years) since I decided that I would give Pratchett the benefit of the doubt and actually read them again prior to writing up a commentary, and this isn't even the last of the Discworld novels on my 'to read' list (I think there are another six, which would bring it up to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47994.The_Last_Continent__Discworld___22__Rincewind__6_" title="The Last Continent (Discworld, #22; Rincewind #6) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Continent</a>). Anyway, enough of my pondering over the Terry Pratchett books that I have read because I think it is time to say a few things about this particular book.<br><br>	As I was discussing this book with a friend last night we came upon the conclusion that there were a number of things in this book that felt forced, such as the parody of Rock n Roll. While the concept was good, and amusing in a way, I felt that the term 'Music with Rocks In' just seemed a little too forced. It seemed as if Pratchett had come up with another modern phenomena to throw into Discworld but struggled with a suitable name, which suggests that maybe Pratchett's creative juices in regards to Discworld are starting to run out. However, as I suggested above, there are another six books on my to read list (Discworld novels that is) so we will see where they go from there.<br><br>	Soul Music was a little strange in that while <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">wikipedia</a> lists it as a 'Death' novel (that is a novel starring the favourite Discworld character, not the state one enters when one ceases to live) it seemed that Death was a minor character, and the whole Susan Sto Helit storyline was more of a subplot. I say this because he focus of the novel was more on Buddy, Cliff, Glod, and their Music with Rocks In band. To me it felt more like Moving Pictures, in that a new idea arrives in Anhk-Morpork and takes the city by storm, which is the modern phenomena known as 'Rock n Roll'. <br><br>	When I say Rock n Roll, Pratchett is referring to:<br><br><a href="http://youtu.be/ku5UeUT7yIQ" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406378009i/10541216._SY540_.jpg" width="169" height="213" alt="Buddy Holly" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>or:<br><br><a href="http://youtu.be/pVlr4g5-r18" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406378009i/10541217._SY540_.jpg" width="188" height="188" alt="The Beatles" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>as opposed to:<br><br><a href="http://youtu.be/0T1IVyXBGjM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406378009i/10541218._SX540_.jpg" width="235" height="176" alt="Def Leppard" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>or:<br><br><a href="http://youtu.be/Rbm6GXllBiw" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406378009i/10541219._SX540_.jpg" width="268" height="151" alt="Guns n Roses" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>though he does give a tribute to:<br><br><a href="http://youtu.be/EfK-WX2pa8c" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406378009i/10541220._SY540_.jpg" width="153" height="211" alt="The Clash" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and:<br><br><a href="http://youtu.be/pOe9PJrbo0s" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406378009i/10541221.jpg" width="213" height="159" alt="Sex Pistols" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>(You can click on the image to open up a video-clip on Youtube).<br><br>	Well, that is enough of me showing off my limited HTML skills (even though some of the limit is imposed by Goodreads) and time to get back to the book. Considering the content of this book (and others like it) I sometimes wonder whether Pratchett has a conservative outlook on life since, once again, we have a modern phenomena invading Discworld and by the end this phenomena is defeated and Discworld goes back to being your normal (or not so normal) fantasy world. In Moving Pictures we had an invasion of, well, moving pictures, and in Reaperman we had an invasion of shopping centres. In another sense it could simply be satire, and here were have Pratchett taking aim at the music industry, especially with CMOT Dibbler successfully (or not so successfully since he doesn't get any of the money) profiting heavily off of the band (we have five thousand dollars for Dibbler, and out of that comes our cut of twenty dollars).<br><br>	I guess in another sense Pratchett is using the absurdity of Discworld to poke fun at the absurdity of modern life, in this case being rock n roll music. The phenomena that arose in the fifties saw a change in the way music was performed. Then again there was not actually all that much of a change. I guess what changed is the style of music in that prior to the fifties much of the popular music, such as jazz, was played in pubs and clubs, while classical music would be played in the concert halls. What musicians like Elvis and The Beatles did was take the popular music out of the club and moved it to the concert hall (or more fittingly the outdoor stage). Where as before you had huge orchestras performing in concert halls, the number of musicians suddenly shrank significantly, usually hovering between three to five. Then there was the mass marketing of music, and this came about with the development of the record player, the radio, and then the television (though while record players had been around for quite a while, we suddenly begin to see them in every home).<br><br>	What I guess Pratchett is really poking fun at here is the effect that the music seemed to have on people. As Pratchett points out, applause would begin at one spot and then radiate out, however when the Band with Rocks In arrived on stage, the entire crowd erupted simultaneously. We have the wizards changing hairstyles and clothes (with one wearing a leather jacket with 'Born to Rune' studded on the back, and this jacket plays a rather interesting role at the end of the book) and we have fans going absolutely crazy when the music is played. In fact that is the key to the antagonist in this book: music changes people - in fact the music has a life of its own.<br><br>	Where does Death fit into all of this. Well, the book opens with Death, and it closes with Death, and it seems that Death is going through another of his crises. I would suggest that it is a mid-life crisis, but this is Death we are talking about, and he is technically not mortal (and as such cannot have a 'mid-life crisis', but rather is a personification of an idea. This time it is the realisation that he cannot forget anything, so he goes on a quest to learn how to forget. Obviously, when he goes off on his merry adventures somebody needs to fill in the void, which is where Susan Sto-Hellit comes into the picture, the daughter of Mort and Ysabell. In fact, what we discover that sixteen years (or longer) has passed since the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/386372.Mort__Discworld___4__Death___1_" title="Mort (Discworld, #4; Death, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Mort</a>, which is longer than the amount of time that passed between the publication of Mort (1987) and this book (1994).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11601336864228795829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363764415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7535528713862246737">This is a classic Discworld novel that continues the Death books, introduces us to Susan Death, and lots and lots of rock music puns. I'm sorry, I mean Music With Rocks In. When a new music craze sweeps Ankh-Morpork and surrounding communities it shakes up everything, and meddles in the affairs of Death. Death's friends and family are determined to sort out what's going on, as Death himself seems to have wandered off again. A fun and witty book with more wordplay than usual, though I'd be remiss</span>
  <span id="freeText7535528713862246737" style="display:none">This is a classic Discworld novel that continues the Death books, introduces us to Susan Death, and lots and lots of rock music puns. I'm sorry, I mean Music With Rocks In. When a new music craze sweeps Ankh-Morpork and surrounding communities it shakes up everything, and meddles in the affairs of Death. Death's friends and family are determined to sort out what's going on, as Death himself seems to have wandered off again. A fun and witty book with more wordplay than usual, though I'd be remiss if I didn't note the unfortunate sign at the Curry Gardens restaurant in Ankh-Morpork, which mixes up the Ls and Rs so it reads like a racist caricature of a Chinese accent from retro TV. It's a blink-and-you'll-miss-it couple of sentences in the book but is certainly not the only instance of its type in Discworld and it's important to note it's not cool.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7535528713862246737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ol7LnqNw6jsUwSsnUIKmUBoBPg0OJ0wXio5STz+RNgGYeKJMGC4jU7Pqn0and6yPzF7ZxcCqwnDR8BT+8tLEmw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G2JEYqWnUU6LSvNTep5DZDkL1OBtbgdswZ/kgCP9Nw0hRC2wHvmYJixhRzKNa0m771QzKKPjiQua4aIx7r7Flw==')})
  }

The Kaids own the biggest ranch in these parts, but he isn’t like his brothers. He speaks strangely, and clearly doesn’t understand much about people. When he asks her to train him to be more human, she knows she’s in over her head. No wonder she understands him. Sam shows her an animal side that her horse training only begins to prepare her for. Damaged monster. So why does she feel so safe around him?\n\nSam Kaid doesn’t know much about himself anymore. Most of his memories come from the last three years, when he was living in the woods and obeying the orders of a murderous alpha. He’s convinced that he will never fit into the legacy his brothers are building, because he’s not like them anymore. All he knows is fighting. When he takes a broken horse to a beautiful local horse trainer, Cassidy, he knows he’s stumbled onto someone important. She sees him. She gets him. She’s patient with his animal ways.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p3/1654.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry Pratchett
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
35,100
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13342804243957968213">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText13342804243957968213" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13342804243957968213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
